## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (deterministic population dynamics / mathematical biology)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by current population size P and possibly explicit time dependence t, matching classical ODE models in population ecology. Common relationships encode density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects, harvesting/immigration, and environmental forcing over time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, per-capita rate constant)
- Linear time-trend in per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradually changing environment or management)
- Exponential time-change in per-capita rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (rapidly improving/worsening conditions)
- Logistic growth ODE (density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (single carrying capacity with K = 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (flexible approach to carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerates roughly with log-distance to capacity)
- Ricker-type continuous density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (strong crowding effects via exponential suppression)
- Birth saturation minus death (net growth): dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (crowded birth process with linear mortality)
- Allee effect (bistability / critical density): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P and high P)
- Constant harvesting/stocking: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed removal/addition independent of P)
- Proportional harvesting (exploitation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (removal proportional to population size)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (periodic environment affecting growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Carrying-capacity behavior often implies dP_dt has a stable zero at a positive P (root structure like (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)^k)).
- Allee effects show two positive equilibria (one unstable threshold, one stable), often requiring a factor like (c*P - 1) in dP_dt.
- Per-capita growth rate diagnostics: if (dP_dt / P) decreases with P, expect negative density dependence via linear, power, log, or exp(-c*P) terms.
- Gompertz-type dynamics are suggested when per-capita growth depends on log(c/P), producing slow approach near the upper equilibrium without a simple quadratic term.
- Harvesting/immigration introduces additive offsets: constant removal/addition appears as -c or +c in dP_dt, shifting equilibria and possibly causing extinction thresholds.
- Seasonality or cyclic resources typically appear as sinusoidal modulation of the intrinsic rate: (c0 + c1*sin(c2*t)) multiplying P and/or density-dependence terms.
- Nonstationary environments can be captured by time-varying parameters (c0 + c1*t, exp(c*t), or rational-in-t modifiers), leading to drifting equilibria over t.
- Strong crowding or interference competition is often better fit by exponential suppression in P (e.g., exp(-c*P)) than by simple quadratic crowding.

Best expression     : P*c0 + c1*log(c2*exp(P*c3) + 1) + c4 + c5*(c6*Abs(P) + c7*t + 1)**c8
Structure desc      : Additive combination of (i) a small linear term in P, (ii) a nested log(1 + c2·exp(c3 P)) nonlinearity, (iii) a constant offset, and (iv) a large-amplitude power law in an affine function of (|P|, t). P enters linearly (c0 P), inside exp(c3 P) within the log, and via Abs(P) inside the power base; t enters only linearly in that base and not in the log term. With c3=-0.912, the log term behaves like ~0.313·(c2 e^{-0.912 P}) for large positive P (small contribution) but grows roughly linearly in |P| for sufficiently negative P; meanwhile the power term has huge scale c5≈97.8 and a strong negative exponent c8=-4.60, so it dominates and decays rapidly as (−0.919|P|+4.067 t+1) grows, but can blow up if that base approaches 0 (suggesting strong sensitivity/possible domain constraints). Approximate behavior: output is largely controlled by 97.8·(4.067 t + 1 − 0.919|P|)^{-4.60} plus a modest asymmetric-in-P log component and a tiny 0.0131·P trend around the offset −0.241.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG21)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P/t**c6
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,P)=0.1404201690960543\;(-1+P/4.5321236760653205)\,(1-P/78.49071311458529)\,P\;+\;0.1404201690960543\; \frac{P}{t^{4.5321236760653205}}.
\]
Key structural facts:

- It is **linear in \(P/t^{4.532...}\)** (a separable term \(P\cdot t^{-a}\) with a non-integer exponent \(a\approx 4.532\)).
- The remaining part is a **cubic polynomial in \(P\)** (since \(P\cdot(-1+P/A)\cdot(1-P/B)\) expands to a cubic).
- There are **no logs, exponentials in \(P\) or \(t\)**, no trig, no absolute values, no rational-in-\(P\) denominators, no piecewise/Max, etc.

So any matching candidate must be able (by parameter choices) to reduce exactly to “cubic in \(P\) + \(P/t^{a}\)”.

Now check each candidate.

1. \(P c0 + c1\log(\cdots)+c4+c5(\cdots)^{c8}\). Contains a log in \(P\) and a power of an affine function of \(t\) and \(|P|\). You can zero out log and power terms, but then you only get an affine function in \(P\) plus constant, not cubic nor \(P/t^a\). **No**.

2. Similar: linear \(P\) terms + log + power. Can’t create cubic in \(P\) nor \(P/t^a\) without introducing forbidden structures. **No**.

3. Adds \(c4|P|\). Absolute value cannot equal a polynomial for all real \(P\) unless coefficient is 0; then same issue as (1). **No**.

4. Log with \(P c3 + c4 t\) in exponent and a power term. Not reducible to cubic + \(P/t^a\). **No**.

5. Same type as (4). **No**.

6. Mix of \(P\exp(t)\log(t)\), \(P\log(1+c5/P)\), exponentials in \(t\), and \(P^{-1/3}\). None can become \(P/t^{4.532}\) for all \(t\); also introduces non-polynomial \(P\)-dependence. **No**.

7. Has \(P\exp(Pc5)\) etc. Exponential in \(P\) cannot become polynomial for all \(P\) unless coefficient 0, then structure still wrong. **No**.

8. Linear in \(P\) plus \(P t\), exponentials, \(P^{-1/3}\). Cannot produce \(P/t^{a}\) (a negative power of \(t\)) without logs/powers of \(t\) in denominator; also lacks cubic in \(P\). **No**.

9. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), \(P\exp(t)\), \(P^{c4}\), and \(\exp(t)\sin(\cdot)\). You could try to set trig and exp terms to 0, leaving a polynomial in \(P\), but then you can at best get a combination of \(P^2, P, P^{c4}\). To match a cubic polynomial you’d need \(c4=3\) and also a \(P^2\) term and \(P\) term—possible for the cubic part. However there is **no way to also get** the separate \(P/t^{4.532}\) term (no negative power of \(t\) anywhere). **No**.

10. Has \(P e^{t}\), \(P\), \(P^{c3}\), \(e^{t}\), and \(\log(P)\log(t)\). No \(t^{-a}\) term; logs/exp must be killed, leaving only polynomial in \(P\) but then missing \(P/t^{a}\). **No**.

11. Similar to (6)/(8): includes \(P\exp(t)\log(t)\), exponentials, and \(P^{-1/3}\). Cannot equal \(P/t^{4.532}\) for all \(t\). **No**.

12. \(P c0 + P c1 e^{t}\log(t) + e^{t} + e^{t}/P^{1/3}\). No cubic in \(P\); also wrong \(t\)-dependence. **No**.

13. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), and \(P\exp(Pc3)\) plus exponentials and \(P^{-1/3}\). Exponential in \(P\) must be zeroed, then no cubic and no \(P/t^a\). **No**.

14. Has \(P^2\), rational \(P c1/(P+c2)\), \(P\log(\cdots/(c5+|P|)+1)\), and \(P^{c7}e^{t}\). Not reducible to pure polynomial + \(P/t^a\). **No**.

15. Has \(P^2\), linear \(P\), and \(P\exp(Pc4)\) plus exponentials and \(P^{-1/3}\). Same obstruction. **No**.

16. Similar to (13)/(15). **No**.

17. Entire expression is a sum of terms all divided by \((P^5+c1)\). GT has no such denominator; to remove it for all \(P\) you’d need numerator proportional to \(P^5+c1\), but numerator here is a mix of \(P^6\), \(P^5 e^{t}\), \(P e^{Pc4}\), etc. Also cannot produce \(P/t^{a}\). **No**.

18. Has \(P/(P+c1)\), \(P\exp(Pc4)\), \(P^{c5}e^{t}\), \(|P|\), constant. Not match. **No**.

19. Same as (18) without \(|P|\)/const. Still wrong. **No**.

20. Same issues: rational in \(P\), exponential in \(P\), and \(P^{c6}e^{t}\). **No**.

21. Same as (19) plus constant. **No**.

22. Polynomial terms up to \(P^3\) plus \(P/(P+c4)\) plus \(P^{c7}e^{t}\). You could kill the rational and exponential terms, leaving a polynomial up to cubic—this could match the cubic-in-\(P\) part. But again there is **no mechanism for \(P/t^{4.532}\)**. **No**.

23. All terms divided by \((P+c2)\) and multiplied by \(e^{c1 t}\) in some parts. Cannot become polynomial + \(P/t^a\). **No**.

24. Polynomial in \(P\) plus \(P\log(c6/(P+c7)+1)\) plus \(e^{t}\). Log/rational structure cannot be removed while still generating \(P/t^a\); also no \(t^{-a}\). **No**.

25. Has \(P/(P+c1)\), \(P/(Pc3+1)\), \(P e^{Pc5}\), \(P^{c6}e^{t}\), constant. Not match. **No**.

26. Same as (25) without constant. **No**.

27. Linear in \(P\) plus \(P/(P+c3)\) plus \(P^{c5}e^{t}\) plus \(e^{t}\). No \(t^{-a}\), and rational/exponential mismatch. **No**.

28. Similar. **No**.

29. Has \(P\) and \(P t\), log(exp(P+ t)), and \(e^{P+t}\log(|P|)\). Not match. **No**.

30. Has \(P e^{t}\log(|P|)\), exponentials, and \(\sin(P\cdot)\). Not match. **No**.

31. Has \(P e^{t}\log(t)\), \(e^{t}\), constant, and \(e^{t}/P^{1/3}\). No cubic and wrong \(t\)-dependence. **No**.

32. No \(P\) in most terms except none; includes exponentials/logs in \(t\). Cannot match GT’s explicit \(P\)-factor structure. **No**.

33. Has \(P/(P+c1)\), \(P e^{Pc4}\), \(P t\), \(P^{c7}e^{t}\). Not match. **No**.

34. Has \(P e^{Pc2}\), \(P^{c3}\), \(e^{t}\), and \(\log(P)\log(t)\). Not match. **No**.

35. Has \(P/(Pc2+1)\) and logs. Not match. **No**.

36. Has \(P^{c0}\) and various exp/log products. Not match. **No**.

37. Has \(P/(P+c1)\), \(P e^{t}\), \(P^{c4}e^{t}\), and \(e^{t}\log(t)\). Not match. **No**.

38. Has \(P e^{t}\log(t)\), \(P\), \(e^{t}\), and \(e^{t}/P^{1/3}\). Not match. **No**.

39. Has \(P^{c0}\), \(P^{c2}\log(t)\), \(e^{t}\), and \(\log(P)\log(t)\). Not match. **No**.

40. Has \(P/(P+c1)\), \(P^{c2}e^{t}\), and a rational-in-\(P\) saturation term \(P^{c5}/(P^{c5}+c7)\). Not match. **No**.

41. Has \(P\) plus \(P^{c1}e^{t}\) plus cosine term and \(e^{t}\). Not match. **No**.

42. Has \(P e^{t}\), \(P^{c2}\), constant, \(e^{t}\), and \(\log(P)\log(t)\). Not match. **No**.

43. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), plus purely \(t\)-dependent exponentials/logs/powers. Even if you match the cubic part (you can’t; no \(P^3\) term), you still can’t get \(P/t^{a}\). **No**.

44. Has \(P e^{t}\), \(P^{c2}\), \(e^{t}\), and \(\log(P)\log(t)\). Not match. **No**.

45. Has \(P e^{P}\) and a Max(0,…) piecewise factor. GT is smooth polynomial/rational in \(t\). Not match. **No**.

46. Has \(P t\), \(P^{c2}\), \(e^{t}\), and \(\log(P)\log(t)\). Not match. **No**.

47. Similar to (46) without \(Pt\). Not match. **No**.

48. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), \(P\), plus \(P^{c3}\log(t)\) and \(e^{t}\). Not match. **No**.

49. Has \(P\) plus \(P^{c1}\) plus \(e^{t}\) plus \(\log(P)\log(t)\). Not match. **No**.

50. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), \(P\), plus \(P^{c3}\log(t)\) and \(e^{t}\). Not match. **No**.

Crucially, **none** of the candidates contains a term that can be tuned to exactly \(P/t^{4.532123676...}\) (a non-integer negative power of \(t\) multiplying \(P\)) while simultaneously keeping the rest as a cubic polynomial in \(P\) with no extra functional forms.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG21)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P/t**c6
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(t, P) = 0.1404 \cdot (-1 + P/4.532) \cdot (1 - P/78.49) \cdot P + 0.1404 \cdot P / t^{4.532}$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) = -1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)$$

So the GT becomes:
$$0.1404 \cdot P \cdot \left(-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)\right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

$$= 0.1404 \cdot \left(-P + P^2/78.49 + P^2/4.532 - P^3/(355.7) \right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

The GT has the form:
$$\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P + \delta P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

where $\alpha, \beta, \gamma, \delta$ are specific constants. The key basis functions are:
- $P^3$
- $P^2$  
- $P$
- $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$

The $t$-dependence is specifically $P/t^{4.532}$, which is $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$.

Now I need to check each candidate for the ability to produce these exact basis functions.

**Key observations about GT structure:**
1. Polynomial in P: cubic ($P^3, P^2, P$)
2. $t$-dependence: $P \cdot t^{-c}$ where $c \approx 4.532$

Let me check candidates that could potentially match. I need candidates with:
- $P^3$ term
- $P^2$ term  
- $P$ term
- $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$ term (or equivalent)

Most candidates use $\exp(ct)$, $\log(ct+1)$, $\sin$, $\cos$, $P^{1/3}$, $\exp(P \cdot c)$, $\log(\exp(...)+1)$ etc. None of these can produce $t^{-4.532}$ exactly.

The term $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$ is a power law in $t$. Let me look for candidates that could produce this.

**Candidates with $(...)^{c}$ terms:**
- Candidates 1-5: have $(c \cdot |P| + c \cdot t + 1)^c$ — this mixes P and t in a power, can't separate into $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$
- Candidate 43: has $(c_8 t + 1)^{c_9}$ — this is a pure $t$ power but not multiplied by $P$

**Candidates with $P^c$ terms (power of P):**
- Candidates 22, 27, 28, etc. have $P^{c} \cdot c \cdot \exp(c \cdot t)$ — exponential in $t$, not power law

**Candidates with $\exp(ct)$:** These produce exponential $t$-dependence, not power law $t^{-4.532}$.

**Candidates with $\log(ct+1)$:** These produce logarithmic $t$-dependence.

None of the candidates contain a term like $P \cdot t^{-c}$ or $P/t^c$. The GT requires a power-law dependence on $t$, and no candidate has this structure.

Let me double-check every candidate... None have $t^c$ or $1/t^c$ as a basis function. They all use $\exp(ct)$, $\log(ct+1)$, $\sin(ct)$, $\cos(ct)$, or polynomial combinations. None can produce $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$.

Since the $t$-dependence in the GT ($P/t^{4.532}$) cannot be replicated by any candidate's available basis functions (exponentials, logs, trig functions), none of the candidates can match the GT.

Candidate 1 through 50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.
